<![endif]--><strong><span style="font-size:13.5pt">Early Identification and Promising Interventions in Adolescence (focus on ages 11-21)</span></strong><span style="font-size:13.5pt">*:</span><span style="font-size:10.0pt">&nbsp; </span>Adolescence opens a window of developmental opportunity. However, both cumulative and current experiences of adversity and trauma during this period may increase vulnerability for negative social and health outcomes. Speakers will discuss the effects of adversity and stressors during adolescence, how to identify them and considerations for interventions that capitalize on developmental opportunities during this period.</li></ul><p style="margin-left:120px"><a href="http://www.aces-ca.org/2016speakers#CHOPEL">Alison Chopel, Director, California Adolescent Health Collaborative, Public Health Institute</a></p><p style="margin-left:120px"><a href="http://www.aces-ca.org/2016speakers#MARTINEZ"><span style="font-size:13.5pt">William Martinez, Fellow, University of California Berkeley</span></a></p><p style="margin-left:120px"><a href="http://www.aces-ca.org/2016speakers#SCHAPIRO">Naomi Schapiro, Clinical Professor, UCSF School of Nursing</a></p><p style="margin-left:120px">Moderated by Juan Taizan, Associate Director Programs, California School-based Health Alliance</p><ul style="margin-left:80px"><li><strong>Addressing the Determinants of ACEs/Toxic Stress*: </strong><span style="font-size:13.5pt">Some communities experience childhood adversity more extremely and profoundly than others. In this interactive session, speakers will present a framework for understanding and addressing community-level trauma and share strategies for developing a multi-sector approach focused on primary prevention.</span></li></ul><p style="margin-left:120px"><!--[if gte mso 9]><xml>

Learn how this news and social media network is helping communities across the country get organized, share resources, and tell their stories as they implement trauma-informed and resilience-building practices. ACEs Connection staff will provide an overview of the network, including its tools, review the types of geographic and interest-based groups on the network, and explain how to start and manage a group for your own community. Members of communities that have groups on <a target="_blank" href="http://www.acesconnection.com/">ACEsConnection.com</a> will explain how they use its tools to support their efforts to create change at local and state levels, including how to post blogs, organize events, recruit and communicate with members and use the networkâ€™s tools to map the community. Whether youâ€™re a current member, or learning about ACEs Connection Network for the first time, this session has something to offer you. Bring your laptop, tablet, or other device to access the site during this session.</li></ul><p style="margin-left:120px"><a href="http://www.aces-ca.org/2016speakers#NETWORK">ACEs Connection Network</a></p><ul style="margin-left:80px"><li><strong>Trauma-informed Systems and Workforce Development (Parts 1 &amp; 2):</strong> A trauma-informed approach uses knowledge of trauma to shape policies and practices across the full range of environments, systems and agencies. Cultivating trauma-informed systems requires a shift in paradigm to include a shared language, common agenda and collective action among the various stakeholders. In part 1 of this session, speakers will discuss the conceptual definitions informing the development of trauma-informed systems. Building off of this overview, in part 2, speakers will look more closely at the application of these perspectives. Participants are encouraged to attend part 1 and part 2.</li></ul><p style="margin-left:120px"><strong>Part 1: </strong><strong>Defining a trauma informed system</strong></p><p style="margin-left:1.25in"><a href="http://www.aces-ca.org/2016speakers#ACEVES"><span style="font-size:13.5pt">Kimberly Aceves, Executive Director, RYSE</span></a></p><p style="margin-left:120px"><a href="http://www.aces-ca.org/2016speakers#JUAREZ">Maretta Juarez, </a><a href="#">Senior Mental Health Program Manager,&nbsp;Santa Clara County Behavioral Health Services Department Family &amp; Childrenâ€™s Division</a><a href="http://www.aces-ca.org/2016speakers#JUAREZ">, Trauma Transformed Collaborative</a></p><p style="margin-left:120px">Moderated by Steve Wirtz, Chief, Injury Surveillance and Epidemiology Section, Safe and Active Communities Branch, California Department of Public Health (CDPH)</p><p style="margin-left:80px">* Indicates session is repeated in Session II</p><p>3:00pm &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
